< text>
I have been here several times and yes the view is amazing and the wine is tasty! A couple things I haven't seen mentioned in other reviews-
First, you need a reservation to get in for a tasting.  So plan ahead! Bring snacks cause you will want to linger.
Second, they offer organic wines and the land is biodynamically farmed! So inspiring.
Third, the gardens are gorgeous (lots of lavender and rosemary) and worth a stroll.
Fourth, there is a generous flat grassy area down below the tasting patio to picnic with your bottle.  We had a great afternoon with our kids there running around on the grass, coming back to the picnic blanket for a snack all while we relaxed and drank our wine.<//text>

<review>Demetria is by far and away my favourite winery in the area. The winery is, in fact, open from 11am-5pm. The signs and website show "by appointment only", but realistically all you have to do is buzz them at the entrance gate and they'll let you in. The appointments are helpful since the number of tables are limited (I think they have maybe 8-10 tables, 2-3 that accommodate 8-10 people) and it tends to get very busy, especially on weekends and in the spring/summer and its a popular venue for events and weddings (which means the winery would be closed to public that day). The scenery and views are breathtaking on the drive up from the gate and at the winery itself.  The wines are superb - I highly recommend the ros√© (both sparkling and regular) and the pinot noirs.  The tasting room staff are incredibly nice and give great explanations and information about the wine.  The experience at Demetria makes you feel like you're family.<//review><pictures>None<//pictures><resp>None< /resp>< gmapID>
0x80ebf8d42dddef19:0xa5270c0d8bd79d78<//gmapID>

I was born and raised in the Napa Valley, the location alone says enough.  However, upon discovering Demetria, the location, the owners and staff, I was enlightened in a brand new way.  No offense to my home turf, but Demetria blows away most Wineries in Napa.  It's the perfect blend of seclusion, mixed with an Italian countryside feel and the staff is BEYOND friendly, always making you feel like friend and family.< /text>

Morgan Burton< /name>
<time>1547274283186<//time>< rating>
4<//rating>
<review>Discovered The Kroft on a whim while searching for something different to eat. It is part of the Union Market, which has a number of interesting businesses tucked away around corners and down narrow lanes.

The Kroft, however, is an excellent and unique place to find delicious comfort food. They specialize in poutine with a fusion twist. The staff were friendly and helpful in explaining the menu. I ordered a fried chicken poutine with brussels sprouts, thinking that the combination would be only be just enough food for one person. I wasn't prepared for the enormous platter of poutine I received - it's a very generous portion that almost requires two to share! Gooey, salted cheese curds mixed very well with the fried popcorn chicken pieces drenched in thick, Southern-style gravy. The brussels sprouts were only okay - a little burned and tart for me, but the presentation was nice.

I'll be back to Union Market to try additional restaurants, but I want to return to The Kroft again for the curry chicken poutine!<//review>< Pics>

<Text>The Kroft is my go-to place when I feel like splurging (calories-wise). All the items here are delicious. My favorite is their Country Fried Chicken Poutine. You can't go wrong with white gravy, fried chicken, fries and cheese curds. Be prepared to drink a lot of water, because the combination of all these goodness can be on the salty side.

My husband ordered the braised beef sandwich and he loved it. The beef was flavorful and tender. They bread doesn't get soggy with the juicy meat (which is a good thing).

If you're not ready to commit to a full order of poutine, I highly recommend getting an order of flaming hot cheese curds. They are delicious.</Text><Pics>None</Pics><Resp>None<//Resp>< gmap_id>

<UserId.>109815267831202318650<//UserId.>< review>
Oh Canada with your Maple Syrup, Hockey, smoked meats and of course the Poutine.

Originating from Quebec it really came over from England in other forms until it was refined. I mean after all this is a cold weather food meant to thicken the blood if you know what I'm saying. That there is the main difference between Canadian Poutine and the offerings here. Most of their menu is fusion of other flavors like the Chicken Katsu curry and the homage to Japanese dish. Mediterranean version of course for it's name sake. The gravy is to be thick enough to cover, but thin enough to seep down between the fries. I find it a little thin here, perfect salting and seasoning, but it's simply lacking the meatiness of the real thing.

The fries, nope not Kennebec, but that's not my biggest concern. It's the doneness of the fries. They consistently cook to a very Socal-esque level. I need real crisp, but having Kennebec would solve this. Anyhow it's like using big old Idaho russets in creole cooking. Not authentic. You must ask for a double fry, it needs to keep some crisp after gravy is poured. I do like the shaved garnishes, makes it fancy-ish.

Portions are about right, certainly not hearty enough for post drinking needs. Prices are a tad high, but the flavor profiles they are going for are higher end too. An odd balance there.

The cheese curds are plenty and flavorful. If they indeed are using fresh, local, organic, sustainable and seasonal ingredients the cheese would really pop. I get an egg on everything, literally. Gravy and egg yolk to me is on that mother sauce level.

Love the loco moco, to me more substantial than the braised short rib. I was hoping for an oxtail offering special . Short rib sandwich is much better, it's a more round profile, the bread has decent crust. Fried chicken sandwich was an item I was surprised I liked so much. Friend chicken poutine is interesting, but the cheese curds don't work the same with the different gravy. More of a b√©chamel versus gravy would solve both the flavors they are trying to mix. The bacon ideally should stay crispy along with the fries, they need to work on that.

Pot pie is a bit thin, chunky, but thin, not enough vegetable flavor considering they really want to go for a true filling topping. Fried cheese curds need a more acidic sauce offering.

I do not like the small boxes they serve in. It's supposed to be filling, like you can't eat a sandwich and poutine, but that's what I need to fill up here.

Great drinks, great service, they have taken to heart my many suggestions to improve most of their items and I see many of the upgrades to be integrated, I've probably told workers at both locations 30 different upgrades they could do to improve their dishes. Fusion is always better when you understand both sides of the dishes or cultures your combining. Too many poutine places I've been to the owners went to Canada once and dove right in and opened a poutinery. Not here, they are evolving, while keeping it regional.

It's a much nicer, bigger space. They offer some beer, but have refreshing drinks, but they really do out draw most of the rest of the shops here. You can catch me here for lunch twice a week and dinner once a week. See you soon, I'll be the guy with the customized orders.< /review>

Luke S.</user_name>
< Date>
1577832760682</Date>
< rating>
5<//rating>
< text>
I've been going to this place since I was a kid. I'm still going as an adult, which says a lot. When I was a kid I didn't really have much of a say over which bagel place we went to nor did I really care. I just wanted a bagel, it didn't matter where I was getting that bagel, unless I had to go super far away for that bagel or if it was a place that didn't specialize in making bagels. Like if I got a bagel from a place that mainly sells burritos or pho and they sold bagels on the side...that probably wouldn't be a great bagel. Pretty much my criteria as a kid for bagels was a place that was close and specialized in making bagels. The Daily Bagel Cafe has both of those things. It's only a 10 min drive away and you know they specialize in making bagels if "bagel" is literally part of their name.

As I got older, I started making more decisions for myself, which meant trying other bagels from other bagel shops. Throughout my lifetime I've tried many bagels from many different bagel shops. Even after going through so many other bagels, I still think Daily Bagel Cafe has the best bagels. They were my favorite when I was a kid, they are my favorite now, and they'll probably be my favorite till I die.< /text>

I've always seen this place on my way home and it wasn't until I took my mom that I realized I had been missing out. I give it 5 stars because it's just so convenient being around the corner from me. It's hidden but not hard to find. When you walk it you're immediately greeted and you're able to seat yourself. Service is prompt and kind. The food is really good! I've had their breakfast burrito and their vegetarian omelet, and although I love hash style potatoes their country potatoes are deliciously seasoned and are cut potato chip style which allows them to be cooked better. This location is not a reflection of the other Waffle Shops I have been to and enjoyed, and maybe they were just having a bad morning at this location. This was my first time to this location so it's all I have to rate it on........ From where my table was I could see into the kitchen and proceeded to watch one of the cooks only wearing one glove while working, while the other cooks had on two. This cook while wearing the same glove wiped counters, handled the broom stick and swept. Then proceeded to use that glove hand to handle plates and utensils while using his bare hand to take the waffles off the grill and put them on the plates. I watched all this for at least 20mins, and he never changed the glove or washed his hand(s) between activities. And while all this was happening another staff memeber was constantly yelling loudly at the busboy to clean tables faster, even though he was the only one doing tables for the whole place during a busy morning. And then when my food finally came my gf's omelette was cool to the touch and the cheese wasn't melted. They poured strawberries out of a jar onto my waffle, that had already been handled with a bare hand, causing it to be the consistency of bread sitting in water. So needless to say we did not eat our food and left. I try very hard to not leave bad reviews because I believe a business is trying their best and bad reviews can hurt a families well being, but what I saw that morning was ridiculous.< /text>

<Time>1498263788776<//Time><Name>Tifanie Henson< /Name>< text>
I have 3 stars because I think it could have been better all around. My son had a dentist appointment across the lot so aftwards we stopped in for breakfast. I looked the shop up on Google before we went. Just to read some reviews, menu prices and such. The prices were good, not too expensive. Once we grabbed a seat and got our menus,  the prices were off, by a couple dollars,  online it read prices around $5-6 a plate, the actual prices were around $8-9!. The waitress was very cold with her greeting and mannerisms. She only came by once to see if everything was ok. And they didn't have a lot of what we were wanting to order. My son wanted a strawberry waffle with vanilla ice cream and a chocolate milk. But they didn't have any ice cream nor chocolate milk.  He ended up with a regular waffle with strawberries and whip cream with a hot chocolate (mind you, here in central California it's 105¬∞ today).  I ordered the waffle combo. (1 waffle, 2 eggs and 3 sausage links) and an iced tea. I ordered the eggs scrambled, they came to the table cold with the sausage that looked burnt. My bill came to $49.81! The only time the waitress was polite was when I was paying the bill. I don't think we will be going back there. It really was not worth $49 for my 14 year old and myself. Especially since we couldn't get what we really wanted to eat. Needless to say,  I did not leave a tip.<//text>
